The Argument for an Ignorant Creator
Deductive argument for an ignorant creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument from God's wisdom leads to positing an ignorant agent (the soul) as the creator of the world.

Core Idea
The world's flaws point to an ignorant creator, not God.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a controversial view attributed to Muhammad ibn Zakariyya (al-Razi) that challenges traditional creation doctrines. The argument attempts to reconcile the existence of evil and imperfection with God's wisdom by proposing that the world was not directly created by God but by an ignorant agent, the soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the logical structure: two premises lead to a conclusion.
2
Identify the premises
Find the two premises: 1) The world is originated (muhdath). 2) The beginning of creation does not befit God's wisdom. What is the logical force of 'لا يليق'?
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that the beginner of the world's origination must be an ignorant agent, identified as the soul. Note that 'ignorant' does not mean foolish but lacking knowledge of outcomes.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this argument is controversial. It attributes the world's flaws to an ignorant agent rather than directly to God, preserving God's wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البالحصة الرابعة
قال ( محمد بن زكرياء » : « لما ثبت بالدليل: أن العالم محدث ، وثبت : أن الابتداء بخلق العالم لا يليق بحكمة الله [ تعالى(۱) ] وجب أن يكون المبتدىء بإحداث العالم فاعلاً جاهلاً ، وذلك هو النفس . وتقريره : أن النفس كانت غافلة عن الهيولى من الأزل إلى الأبد ، ثم اتفق لها التفات إلى الهيولى ، واعتقدت أنها إذا اختلطت بالهيولي قدرت على استيفاء اللذات ، فحصل للنفس عشق طبيعي غريزي على هذه الهيولى ، وهذا العشق لا شك في حصوله . الا ترى أن عشق كل نفس على جسده عشق کامل تام ، لا يمكن حصول عشق أكمل منه ، فلما حصل للنفس ذلك الالتفات الاتفاقي ، والإدراك الغيبي ، وتفرع على حصول ذلك الالتفات حصول هذا [ العشق (۲) ] الغريزي ، لا جرم تعلقت النفس بالهيولى ، وحصل من تركيبها : الحيواني (٣) . وعلم الإله الحكيم أن ذلك التعلق سبب لفتح باب الآفات والشرور والمضار ، وبسبب أن الهيولى لا يقبل التركيب المحكم المتقن ، الخالي عن جميع جهات المضار . إلا أن الباري [ تعالى (٤) ] كما علم ذلك ، علم أيضاً : أنه لا يمكن منع النفس عن
The Fourth Lesson: He (Muhammad ibn Zakariyya) said: Since it is established by proof that the world is originated (muhdath), and it is established that the beginning of the creation of the world is not befitting the wisdom (hikmah) of God – exalted is He – it necessarily follows that the beginner of the origination of the world is an ignorant agent (fa'ilun jahilun), and that is the soul (al-nafs). Its explanation (taqrir) is that the soul was heedless of the hylé (al-hayula) from eternity to eternity, then there occurred to it an accidental turning of attention (iltafat) to the hylé, and it believed that if it mingled with the hylé it would be able to obtain pleasures, so there obtained for the soul a natural instinctive love (ishq tabi'i gharezi) for this hylé, and there is no doubt in the occurrence of this love. Do you not see that the love of every soul for its body is a complete perfect love, the attainment of a love more complete than it is impossible? So when there obtained for the soul that accidental turning of attention and the unseen perception (al-idrak al-ghaybi), and there branched off from the occurrence of that turning of attention the occurrence of this instinctive love, inevitably the soul attached itself (ta'allaqat) to the hylé, and from its composition there resulted the living (al-hayawani) – i.e., anger and desire. And the Wise God (al-ilah al-hakim) knew that that attachment is a cause for opening the door of calamities and evils and harms, and because the hylé does not accept the tight precise composition that is free from all aspects of harm. But the Creator – exalted is He – just as He knew that, He also knew that it is impossible to prevent the soul from
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents and explains an argument attributed to Muhammad ibn Zakariyya (likely the physician and philosopher Abu Bakr al-Razi). It is a proof by reasoning that the world must have been created by an ignorant agent, which is the soul. The argument begins with two premises: first, the world is originated (muhdath) – this is presumably established by some earlier proof; second, it is not befitting God's wisdom (hikmah) to initiate the creation of the world. From these, it concludes that the beginner of the world's origination must be an ignorant agent, and that agent is the soul. Then the author gives a detailed explanation (taqrir) of how this happens. The soul was eternally heedless of prime matter (al-hayula). Then it accidentally turned its attention to the hylé, believing that mixing with it would allow it to obtain pleasures. This generated a natural instinctive love (ishq) for the hylé, which is undeniable. The author illustrates this by pointing to the strong love every soul has for its own body. This love is so perfect that no greater love is possible. Through this accidental attention and unseen perception, the instinctive love arose, and as a result the soul attached itself to the hylé. From their composition came the living being (al-hayawani), which the gloss identifies as anger and desire (i.e., the animal faculties). The Wise God foreknew that this attachment would open the door to evils and harms, and that the hylé cannot receive a perfectly balanced composition free from harm. Nevertheless, God also knew that He cannot prevent the soul from [the text cuts off]. The argument appears to be a theological-philosophical position that is likely being cited for refutation, as the book is by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi who often critiques such views.

محدث
حكمة
نفس
فاعل جاهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument implies God is ignorant.
Correction: The argument explicitly says the agent is ignorant precisely because God's wisdom prohibits direct creation; it preserves God's wisdom by shifting the agency.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why must the beginner of the world's origination be an ignorant agent?
A) Because the world is eternal.
B) Because beginning creation does not befit God's wisdom.
C) Because God is ignorant.
D) Because the soul is the only agent capable of creation.

Key Takeaway
The argument uses the existence of evil to infer an ignorant creator distinct from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness suffering or injustice in the world, do you ever secretly entertain the thought that God must be indifferent or lacking in wisdom? How does Razi's argument—that such creation is 'not befitting God'—either challenge or comfort your doubts? Tonight, confess honestly to God: do you truly believe His wisdom runs deeper than the surface chaos?
?
If the soul (your own soul) is implicated in creating this flawed world through its ignorance, what does that mean for your own moral failures? Is it easier to blame a cosmic soul than to take full responsibility for your choices? Will you today examine one area of your life where you have excused sin by attributing it to 'the way things are' rather than your own will?
?
Razi separates God from the act of creating a world with evil, but the Qur'an says 'He is the Creator of everything' (Q. 6:102). Which of these two perspectives do you find harder to submit to—that God directly creates evil, or that an ignorant soul acts independently? Sincerely ask yourself: are you trying to protect God's reputation at the cost of shrinking His sovereignty? What would it mean for you to trust that both good and evil ultimately come from Him, yet He remains perfectly wise?

The Soul's Accidental Attachment to Matter
Narrative explanation of the soul's attachment to matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mythical narrative of how the soul, originally heedless, becomes attached to matter through accidental attention and love, giving rise to the living being.

Core Idea
The soul's accidental love for matter creates the living world.

After establishing that an ignorant agent (the soul) must have initiated creation, the author now provides a detailed mythological explanation. It depicts the soul as eternally heedless of prime matter (hylé), then accidentally turning its attention to it, leading to love, attachment, and the formation of the living being. This narrative attempts to explain the origin of evil and imperfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation
Read the taqrir (explanation) carefully. It tells a story of the soul's journey from heedlessness to attachment.
2
Identify key concepts
Identify: hylé (prime matter), accidental attention (iltafat ittifaqi), instinctive love (ishq tabi'i), and the living being (al-hayawani).
3
Understand the role of divine foreknowledge
Note that God (al-ilah al-hakim) knows that this attachment will cause harm, but He cannot prevent the soul. What does this imply about God's power?
4
Connect to the overall argument
Reflect on how this narrative fits the conclusion of an ignorant agent. The soul acts ignorantly (accidentally), and the result is a flawed world.

البالحصة الرابعة
قال ( محمد بن زكرياء » : « لما ثبت بالدليل: أن العالم محدث ، وثبت : أن الابتداء بخلق العالم لا يليق بحكمة الله [ تعالى(۱) ] وجب أن يكون المبتدىء بإحداث العالم فاعلاً جاهلاً ، وذلك هو النفس . وتقريره : أن النفس كانت غافلة عن الهيولى من الأزل إلى الأبد ، ثم اتفق لها التفات إلى الهيولى ، واعتقدت أنها إذا اختلطت بالهيولي قدرت على استيفاء اللذات ، فحصل للنفس عشق طبيعي غريزي على هذه الهيولى ، وهذا العشق لا شك في حصوله . الا ترى أن عشق كل نفس على جسده عشق کامل تام ، لا يمكن حصول عشق أكمل منه ، فلما حصل للنفس ذلك الالتفات الاتفاقي ، والإدراك الغيبي ، وتفرع على حصول ذلك الالتفات حصول هذا [ العشق (۲) ] الغريزي ، لا جرم تعلقت النفس بالهيولى ، وحصل من تركيبها : الحيواني (٣) . وعلم الإله الحكيم أن ذلك التعلق سبب لفتح باب الآفات والشرور والمضار ، وبسبب أن الهيولى لا يقبل التركيب المحكم المتقن ، الخالي عن جميع جهات المضار . إلا أن الباري [ تعالى (٤) ] كما علم ذلك ، علم أيضاً : أنه لا يمكن منع النفس عن
The Fourth Lesson: He (Muhammad ibn Zakariyya) said: Since it is established by proof that the world is originated (muhdath), and it is established that the beginning of the creation of the world is not befitting the wisdom (hikmah) of God – exalted is He – it necessarily follows that the beginner of the origination of the world is an ignorant agent (fa'ilun jahilun), and that is the soul (al-nafs). Its explanation (taqrir) is that the soul was heedless of the hylé (al-hayula) from eternity to eternity, then there occurred to it an accidental turning of attention (iltafat) to the hylé, and it believed that if it mingled with the hylé it would be able to obtain pleasures, so there obtained for the soul a natural instinctive love (ishq tabi'i gharezi) for this hylé, and there is no doubt in the occurrence of this love. Do you not see that the love of every soul for its body is a complete perfect love, the attainment of a love more complete than it is impossible? So when there obtained for the soul that accidental turning of attention and the unseen perception (al-idrak al-ghaybi), and there branched off from the occurrence of that turning of attention the occurrence of this instinctive love, inevitably the soul attached itself (ta'allaqat) to the hylé, and from its composition there resulted the living (al-hayawani) – i.e., anger and desire. And the Wise God (al-ilah al-hakim) knew that that attachment is a cause for opening the door of calamities and evils and harms, and because the hylé does not accept the tight precise composition that is free from all aspects of harm. But the Creator – exalted is He – just as He knew that, He also knew that it is impossible to prevent the soul from
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents and explains an argument attributed to Muhammad ibn Zakariyya (likely the physician and philosopher Abu Bakr al-Razi). It is a proof by reasoning that the world must have been created by an ignorant agent, which is the soul. The argument begins with two premises: first, the world is originated (muhdath) – this is presumably established by some earlier proof; second, it is not befitting God's wisdom (hikmah) to initiate the creation of the world. From these, it concludes that the beginner of the world's origination must be an ignorant agent, and that agent is the soul. Then the author gives a detailed explanation (taqrir) of how this happens. The soul was eternally heedless of prime matter (al-hayula). Then it accidentally turned its attention to the hylé, believing that mixing with it would allow it to obtain pleasures. This generated a natural instinctive love (ishq) for the hylé, which is undeniable. The author illustrates this by pointing to the strong love every soul has for its own body. This love is so perfect that no greater love is possible. Through this accidental attention and unseen perception, the instinctive love arose, and as a result the soul attached itself to the hylé. From their composition came the living being (al-hayawani), which the gloss identifies as anger and desire (i.e., the animal faculties). The Wise God foreknew that this attachment would open the door to evils and harms, and that the hylé cannot receive a perfectly balanced composition free from harm. Nevertheless, God also knew that He cannot prevent the soul from [the text cuts off]. The argument appears to be a theological-philosophical position that is likely being cited for refutation, as the book is by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi who often critiques such views.

Key Terms
هيولى
التفات
عشق
الحيواني
إله حكيم
باري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This narrative suggests that God created evil.
Correction: The narrative attributes the origin of evil to the soul's ignorant choice, not to God. God only foreknows but does not prevent, implying a limit on His power, but He is not the author of evil.

Checkpoint
According to the narrative, what causes the soul to attach to the hylé?
A) God's command.
B) Accidental attention and instinctive love.
C) The soul's innate wisdom.
D) The world's perfection.

Key Takeaway
The soul's accidental love for matter is the origin of the physical world and its evils.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel an intense attachment to a worldly desire, can you see the echo of the soul's first accidental turning? What would it cost you to admit that this attachment stems from an ignorant belief, not from genuine need?
?
If the source of evil is your own soul's ignorant love, not God's will, then how will you take responsibility for the harm your attachments cause? Will you continue to blame circumstances, or will you trace your suffering back to your own turning?
?
The Wise God knows that your attachments open doors to harm, yet He does not force you away. Knowing this, what specific attachment in your life are you willing to examine today, and what step will you take to loosen its hold?

Causality and Created Things
advanced
6 min
The Soul as Ignorant Initator of Creation
Razi states the proof for the soul as initiator and the origin of its love.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Muhammad ibn Zakariya uses the accidental turning of the soul to matter as the initial cause of the world, resolving the tension between God's wisdom and the existence of material creation.

Core Idea
The soul's accidental love for matter explains why an imperfect world exists.

This lesson introduces the core of Razi's cosmological argument: the world is originated, but its initiation cannot be directly attributed to a wise agent. Therefore, an ignorant agent—the soul—must have started it. We will explore how this leads to the soul's attachment to matter and the origin of the animal soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof's premises
Start by identifying the two established premises: the world is originated, and initiating it is not befitting divine wisdom. Then see the conclusion that the initiator is an ignorant agent, which is the soul.
This is a classic kalam argument structure.
2
Understand the soul's accidental turn
Notice the key shift: the soul was heedless but accidentally turned to matter, believed it could gain pleasures, and developed an instinctive love. This love is so strong it cannot be removed.
The term 'accidental' (اتفاقي) is crucial—it preserves divine transcendence.
3
Trace the consequence
Follow how this love leads to the soul's attachment and composition with matter, resulting in the animal soul (implying appetite and anger). This is the first level of material existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البالحصة الرابعة
قال محمد بن زكرياء: «لما ثبت بالدليل: أن العالم محدث، وثبت: أن الابتداء بخلق العالم لا يليق بحكمة الله تعالى وجب أن يكون المبتدىء بإحداث العالم فاعلاً جاهلاً، وذلك هو النفس. وتقريره: أن النفس كانت غافلة عن الهيولى من الأزل إلى الأبد، ثم اتفق لها التفات إلى الهيولى، واعتقدت أنها إذا اختلطت بالهيولي قدرت على استيفاء اللذات، فحصل للنفس عشق طبيعي غريزي على هذه الهيولى، وهذا العشق لا شك في حصوله. ألا ترى أن عشق كل نفس على جسده عشق كامل تام، لا يمكن حصول عشق أكمل منه، فلما حصل للنفس ذلك الالتفات الاتفاقي، والإدراك الغيبي، وتفرع على حصول ذلك الالتفات حصول هذا العشق الغريزي، لا جرم تعلقت النفس بالهيولى، وحصل من تركيبها: الحيواني. وعلم الإله الحكيم أن ذلك التعلق سبب لفتح باب الآفات والشرور والمضار، وبسبب أن الهيولى لا يقبل التركيب المحكم المتقن، الخالي عن جميع جهات المضار. إلا أن الباري تعالى كما علم ذلك، علم أيضاً: أنه لا يمكن منع النفس عن ذلك التعلق، لأن العشق قد بلغ في القوة والكمال، إلى حيث لا يمكن إزالته. وعلم الإله الحكيم أيضاً أمراً ثالثاً، وهو: أن النفس لا تقدر على التركيب الجيد، بل لو وقع الاقتصار على ما تتولاه النفس بذاتها، لكانت تلك التركيبات فاسدة، سريعة البطلان. فكان تحصل الآلام الشديدة الكثيرة بسرعة تلك التركيبات، فلما علم الإله الحكيم الرحيم هذه المعاني الثلاثة، علم بأن الأصوب الأصلح: أن تركب الأجسام التي حاولت النفس التعلق بها على التركيب الأقرب إلى الصلاح، والأبعد عن قبول الفساد، حتى تكثر الخيرات، وتقل الآفات، بحسب الإمكان. ثم إنه تعالى يفيض نور العقل على جوهر النفس، حتى يظهر له بسبب نور العقل: أن الآفات الحاصلة في هذا التركيب أكثر من الخيرات الحاصلة فيه فحينئذ ينفر طبع النفس عن الاختلاط بالهيولى، وتعود إلى عالمها فارغة، مطهرة عن الالتفات إلى عالم الهيولى، قال: (وعلى هذا الطريق فتلك الدلائل الثلاثة غير واردة). أما الحجة الأولى: وهي قولهم: إنه كيف يليق بالفاعل أن ينتقل من الترك إلى الفعل لا لحكمة. فهذا غير وارد ههنا. لأن هذا، وإن كان غير لائق بالفاعل الحكيم، إلا أنه لا يليق بالفاعل الجاهل العابث. ثم إذا أقدم الفاعل الجاهل العابث على فعل لا ينبغي، وعلم الفاعل الحكيم أنه لا يمكن دفعه عنه، كان الفاعل الحكيم معذوراً في أن يصرف ذلك الفعل إلى الوجه الأصوب الأصلح فيه بحسب الإمكان.»
The Fourth Section. Muhammad ibn Zakariya said: 'When it is established by proof that the world is originated, and it is established that the beginning of creating the world is not befitting the wisdom of God Almighty, then it must be that the initiator of bringing the world into existence is an ignorant agent, and that is the soul. Its exposition: The soul was heedless of matter from eternity to eternity, then it accidentally turned its attention to matter, and believed that if it mixed with matter, it could attain pleasures. So a natural, instinctive love for this matter occurred in the soul, and this love is beyond doubt. Do you not see that each soul's love for its own body is a complete and perfect love, no more perfect love can occur? So when that accidental turning of attention and that absent perception occurred to the soul, and from that turning of attention resulted this instinctive love, necessarily the soul attached itself to matter, and from its composition resulted the animal [soul]. The wise God knew that this attachment is a cause for opening the door of calamities, evils, and harms, and because matter does not accept a solid, perfect composition free from all aspects of harm. However, the Creator Almighty, just as He knew that, also knew that it is impossible to prevent the soul from that attachment, because love had reached such strength and perfection that it cannot be removed. And the wise God also knew a third thing: that the soul cannot make a good composition; rather, if one were to restrict to what the soul undertakes by itself, those compositions would be corrupt and quickly perishable. Thus severe and numerous pains would occur quickly from those compositions. So when the wise, merciful God knew these three meanings, He knew that the most correct and most beneficial is that the bodies which the soul attempted to attach to should be composed in the composition closest to well-being and farthest from accepting corruption, so that goods multiply and calamities diminish as much as possible. Then He Almighty pours the light of intellect upon the substance of the soul, so that it becomes manifest to it through the light of intellect that the calamities occurring in this composition are more than the goods occurring in it. Then the soul's nature becomes averse to mixing with matter, and it returns to its world empty, purified from attention to the world of matter.' He said: 'And along this path, those three proofs are not valid. As for the first proof, which is their saying: How is it befitting for an agent to move from abandonment to action without a reason? This is not valid here. Because this, although not befitting a wise agent, yet it is not unbecoming for an ignorant, frivolous agent. Then if the ignorant, frivolous agent undertakes an action that is not proper, and the wise agent knows that he cannot prevent him from it, the wise agent is excused in directing that action to the most correct and most beneficial aspect in it as much as possible.'
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents a philosophical proof for the soul as the initial cause of the world and then refutes the first of three objections against it. The proof begins by establishing two premises: (1) the world is originated (hadith), and (2) beginning the creation of the world is not befitting the wisdom of God (who is all-wise). Therefore, the initiator must be an ignorant agent, and that agent is the soul (al-nafs). The author then explains how the soul came to act: it was originally heedless of matter (al-hayula), but accidentally turned its attention to it and believed that mixing with matter would allow it to attain pleasures. This produced a natural, instinctive love (ʿishq) for matter. This love is so strong that it cannot be removed, as seen in the total love each soul has for its own body. Consequently, the soul attached itself to matter, resulting in the animal soul (al-hayawani, i.e., appetite and anger). The wise God (al-ilah al-hakim) then considered three things: First, this attachment causes calamities and evils because matter cannot receive a perfect composition. Second, it is impossible to prevent the soul from this attachment due to the strength of its love. Third, the soul itself cannot make a good composition; its attempts would be corrupt and quickly perishable, causing severe pains. Knowing these three, God in His wisdom and mercy decided to compose the bodies that the soul seeks in the best possible way—closest to well-being and farthest from corruption—to maximize goods and minimize calamities. Additionally, God pours the light of intellect (nur al-ʿaql) onto the soul, so it realizes that the calamities in this composition outweigh the goods, leading it to detach from matter and return to its pure world. The author then addresses the first objection: How can a wise agent (God) allow such a harmful action? The response is that the agent in question is not the wise God but the ignorant, frivolous soul. The wise God, being unable to prevent the soul, is excused in directing the action to the best possible outcome. This refutation preserves divine wisdom while explaining the existence of evil.

Key Terms
النفس (al-nafs)
الهيولى (al-hayula)
العشق (al-'ishq)
الفاعل الجاهل (al-fa'il al-jahil)
التركيب (al-tarkib)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Razi's argument denies divine omnipotence or wisdom.
Correction: Razi does not deny divine wisdom; he argues that the initial move came from the soul's accidental turn, not from God. God's wisdom is then employed to direct the outcome.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the immediate cause of the soul's attachment to matter?
A) God's command
B) The soul's accidental turning and instinctive love
C) The need for the animal soul
D) The soul's inherent wisdom

Key Takeaway
The soul's accidental love for matter, not divine will, initiates the creation of the physical world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pursue a worldly pleasure, do you ever pause to ask whether that desire is rooted in a genuine need or merely an accidental attraction that your soul has latched onto? How would your life change if you examined every craving as the passage does—as a possible consequence of the soul's ignorant love?
?
The passage says the soul's love for matter is 'instinctive and innate'—so strong that it cannot be surpassed. Can you identify one material attachment in your life that feels so natural you have never questioned it? What would it cost you to loosen that attachment and turn your attention back to the heedlessness before the accidental turn?
?
If the imperfection of the physical world stems from the soul's ignorance, not from God's plan, then your own dissatisfaction with life may be a signal that your soul is still trapped in that same love. Are you willing to admit that your deepest frustrations might be the result of your own soul's misdirected longing, and then actively seek to redirect that longing toward its true source?

Causality and Created Things

God's Wise Response to the Soul's Action
Razi describes God's threefold knowledge and His wise plan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi explains that God, knowing the soul's unavoidable attachment, directs the outcome to maximize good and minimize evil, and eventually frees the soul through intellect.

Core Idea
God's wisdom transforms unavoidable chaos into the best possible order.

In the previous lesson, we saw that the soul's accidental love forced it to attach to matter. How does God respond? This lesson shows that God knows three things about this situation and, in His wisdom and mercy, decides to compose the bodies in the best possible way. Additionally, He pours the light of intellect so the soul eventually detaches and returns to its pure world.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three things God knows
Read the passage carefully and list the three things God knew about the soul's attachment: it causes evils, cannot be prevented, and the soul's own compositions would be corrupt.
These three pieces of knowledge justify God's subsequent action.
2
Understand God's decision
God decides to compose the bodies in the best way, maximizing good and minimizing evil as much as possible. This is the 'best possible world' reasoning.
3
Learn about the light of intellect
Notice that God also pours the light of intellect (nur al-'aql) onto the soul so it realizes the balance of evil over good, leading to its detachment and return to its world.
This shows the eventual liberation of the soul.

Source Text

Therefore, the initiator must be an ignorant agent, and that agent is the soul (al-nafs). The author then explains how the soul came to act: it was originally heedless of matter (al-hayula), but accidentally turned its attention to it and believed that mixing with matter would allow it to attain pleasures. This produced a natural, instinctive love (ʿishq) for matter. This love is so strong that it cannot be removed, as seen in the total love each soul has for its own body. Consequently, the soul attached itself to matter, resulting in the animal soul (al-hayawani, i.e., appetite and anger). The wise God (al-ilah al-hakim) then considered three things: First, this attachment causes calamities and evils because matter cannot receive a perfect composition. Second, it is impossible to prevent the soul from this attachment due to the strength of its love. Third, the soul itself cannot make a good composition; its attempts would be corrupt and quickly perishable, causing severe pains. Knowing these three, God in His wisdom and mercy decided to compose the bodies that the soul seeks in the best possible way—closest to well-being and farthest from corruption—to maximize goods and minimize calamities. Additionally, God pours the light of intellect (nur al-ʿaql) onto the soul, so it realizes that the calamities in this composition outweigh the goods, leading it to detach from matter and return to its pure world. The author then addresses the first objection: How can a wise agent (God) allow such a harmful action? The response is that the agent in question is not the wise God but the ignorant, frivolous soul. The wise God, being unable to prevent the soul, is excused in directing the action to the best possible outcome. This refutation preserves divine wisdom while explaining the existence of evil.

Key Terms
الفاعل الحكيم (al-fa'il al-hakim)
الآفات (al-afat)
نور العقل (nur al-'aql)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the third thing the wise God knows about the soul?
A) The soul's love is weak.
B) The soul cannot make a good composition.
C) The soul is eternal.
D) The soul is ignorant of its own nature.

Key Takeaway
God's wisdom and mercy transform the inevitable flawed attachment into the best possible arrangement, culminating in the soul's liberation through intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals that your soul's attachment to the material world, though inevitable, is not a dead end—God's wisdom has designed a path through it. In what specific area of your life are you clinging to a composition (a relationship, career, possession) that brings more harm than good, yet you resist seeing it? What would it mean for you to let the light of intellect expose that imbalance today?
?
Razi says the soul becomes averse to mixing with matter when it truly sees that calamities outweigh goods. When you examine your own pursuits—your habits, your worries, your pleasures—can you honestly say you see that the harms outweigh the benefits? If not, what might be blinding you from this truth? Will you ask the All-Wise to pour His light on that blind spot right now?
?
God knew you could not prevent attachment to this world, so He arranged the best possible course for your purification. Are you cooperating with that divine plan, or are you fighting it by trying to 'compose' your own life according to your desires? What would it mean for you to surrender your own composition to the One whose knowledge and mercy are perfect?

Refuting the First Objection: The Wise Agent's Excuse
Razi refutes the first objection by distinguishing agents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the objection that a wise agent cannot move from inaction to action without a reason, by distinguishing between the ignorant initiator (soul) and the wise manager (God).

Core Idea
A wise agent is excused when he redirects an unavoidable ignorant action to the best possible outcome.

The first objection against the soul-as-initiator theory is: how can a wise agent (God) begin creation without a reason? Razi's answer is clear: God is not the initiator; the soul is. God, as a wise agent, sees an ignorant agent (the soul) about to do harm and intervenes to minimize the damage. This lesson will unpack this defense of divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objection is: it is not befitting for a wise agent to move from not acting to acting without a reason. This seems to apply to God.
This is a standard theological problem.
2
Identify the two agents
Razi distinguishes between the wise agent (God) and the ignorant agent (the soul). The objection only applies to the wise agent, but in this scenario, the initiator is the ignorant soul.
3
Understand the excuse
When the ignorant agent acts improperly, the wise agent, unable to stop him, is excused in directing the action to the best possible outcome. This preserves God's wisdom.
This is a key theodicy move.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البالحصة الرابعة
قال محمد بن زكرياء: «لما ثبت بالدليل: أن العالم محدث، وثبت: أن الابتداء بخلق العالم لا يليق بحكمة الله تعالى وجب أن يكون المبتدىء بإحداث العالم فاعلاً جاهلاً، وذلك هو النفس. وتقريره: أن النفس كانت غافلة عن الهيولى من الأزل إلى الأبد، ثم اتفق لها التفات إلى الهيولى، واعتقدت أنها إذا اختلطت بالهيولي قدرت على استيفاء اللذات، فحصل للنفس عشق طبيعي غريزي على هذه الهيولى، وهذا العشق لا شك في حصوله. ألا ترى أن عشق كل نفس على جسده عشق كامل تام، لا يمكن حصول عشق أكمل منه، فلما حصل للنفس ذلك الالتفات الاتفاقي، والإدراك الغيبي، وتفرع على حصول ذلك الالتفات حصول هذا العشق الغريزي، لا جرم تعلقت النفس بالهيولى، وحصل من تركيبها: الحيواني. وعلم الإله الحكيم أن ذلك التعلق سبب لفتح باب الآفات والشرور والمضار، وبسبب أن الهيولى لا يقبل التركيب المحكم المتقن، الخالي عن جميع جهات المضار. إلا أن الباري تعالى كما علم ذلك، علم أيضاً: أنه لا يمكن منع النفس عن ذلك التعلق، لأن العشق قد بلغ في القوة والكمال، إلى حيث لا يمكن إزالته. وعلم الإله الحكيم أيضاً أمراً ثالثاً، وهو: أن النفس لا تقدر على التركيب الجيد، بل لو وقع الاقتصار على ما تتولاه النفس بذاتها، لكانت تلك التركيبات فاسدة، سريعة البطلان. فكان تحصل الآلام الشديدة الكثيرة بسرعة تلك التركيبات، فلما علم الإله الحكيم الرحيم هذه المعاني الثلاثة، علم بأن الأصوب الأصلح: أن تركب الأجسام التي حاولت النفس التعلق بها على التركيب الأقرب إلى الصلاح، والأبعد عن قبول الفساد، حتى تكثر الخيرات، وتقل الآفات، بحسب الإمكان. ثم إنه تعالى يفيض نور العقل على جوهر النفس، حتى يظهر له بسبب نور العقل: أن الآفات الحاصلة في هذا التركيب أكثر من الخيرات الحاصلة فيه فحينئذ ينفر طبع النفس عن الاختلاط بالهيولى، وتعود إلى عالمها فارغة، مطهرة عن الالتفات إلى عالم الهيولى، قال: (وعلى هذا الطريق فتلك الدلائل الثلاثة غير واردة). أما الحجة الأولى: وهي قولهم: إنه كيف يليق بالفاعل أن ينتقل من الترك إلى الفعل لا لحكمة. فهذا غير وارد ههنا. لأن هذا، وإن كان غير لائق بالفاعل الحكيم، إلا أنه لا يليق بالفاعل الجاهل العابث. ثم إذا أقدم الفاعل الجاهل العابث على فعل لا ينبغي، وعلم الفاعل الحكيم أنه لا يمكن دفعه عنه، كان الفاعل الحكيم معذوراً في أن يصرف ذلك الفعل إلى الوجه الأصوب الأصلح فيه بحسب الإمكان.»
The Fourth Section. Muhammad ibn Zakariya said: 'When it is established by proof that the world is originated, and it is established that the beginning of creating the world is not befitting the wisdom of God Almighty, then it must be that the initiator of bringing the world into existence is an ignorant agent, and that is the soul. Its exposition: The soul was heedless of matter from eternity to eternity, then it accidentally turned its attention to matter, and believed that if it mixed with matter, it could attain pleasures. So a natural, instinctive love for this matter occurred in the soul, and this love is beyond doubt. Do you not see that each soul's love for its own body is a complete and perfect love, no more perfect love can occur? So when that accidental turning of attention and that absent perception occurred to the soul, and from that turning of attention resulted this instinctive love, necessarily the soul attached itself to matter, and from its composition resulted the animal [soul]. The wise God knew that this attachment is a cause for opening the door of calamities, evils, and harms, and because matter does not accept a solid, perfect composition free from all aspects of harm. However, the Creator Almighty, just as He knew that, also knew that it is impossible to prevent the soul from that attachment, because love had reached such strength and perfection that it cannot be removed. And the wise God also knew a third thing: that the soul cannot make a good composition; rather, if one were to restrict to what the soul undertakes by itself, those compositions would be corrupt and quickly perishable. Thus severe and numerous pains would occur quickly from those compositions. So when the wise, merciful God knew these three meanings, He knew that the most correct and most beneficial is that the bodies which the soul attempted to attach to should be composed in the composition closest to well-being and farthest from accepting corruption, so that goods multiply and calamities diminish as much as possible. Then He Almighty pours the light of intellect upon the substance of the soul, so that it becomes manifest to it through the light of intellect that the calamities occurring in this composition are more than the goods occurring in it. Then the soul's nature becomes averse to mixing with matter, and it returns to its world empty, purified from attention to the world of matter.' He said: 'And along this path, those three proofs are not valid. As for the first proof, which is their saying: How is it befitting for an agent to move from abandonment to action without a reason? This is not valid here. Because this, although not befitting a wise agent, yet it is not unbecoming for an ignorant, frivolous agent. Then if the ignorant, frivolous agent undertakes an action that is not proper, and the wise agent knows that he cannot prevent him from it, the wise agent is excused in directing that action to the most correct and most beneficial aspect in it as much as possible.'
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents a philosophical proof for the soul as the initial cause of the world and then refutes the first of three objections against it. The proof begins by establishing two premises: (1) the world is originated (hadith), and (2) beginning the creation of the world is not befitting the wisdom of God (who is all-wise). Therefore, the initiator must be an ignorant agent, and that agent is the soul (al-nafs). The author then explains how the soul came to act: it was originally heedless of matter (al-hayula), but accidentally turned its attention to it and believed that mixing with matter would allow it to attain pleasures. This produced a natural, instinctive love (ʿishq) for matter. This love is so strong that it cannot be removed, as seen in the total love each soul has for its own body. Consequently, the soul attached itself to matter, resulting in the animal soul (al-hayawani, i.e., appetite and anger). The wise God (al-ilah al-hakim) then considered three things: First, this attachment causes calamities and evils because matter cannot receive a perfect composition. Second, it is impossible to prevent the soul from this attachment due to the strength of its love. Third, the soul itself cannot make a good composition; its attempts would be corrupt and quickly perishable, causing severe pains. Knowing these three, God in His wisdom and mercy decided to compose the bodies that the soul seeks in the best possible way—closest to well-being and farthest from corruption—to maximize goods and minimize calamities. Additionally, God pours the light of intellect (nur al-ʿaql) onto the soul, so it realizes that the calamities in this composition outweigh the goods, leading it to detach from matter and return to its pure world. The author then addresses the first objection: How can a wise agent (God) allow such a harmful action? The response is that the agent in question is not the wise God but the ignorant, frivolous soul. The wise God, being unable to prevent the soul, is excused in directing the action to the best possible outcome. This refutation preserves divine wisdom while explaining the existence of evil.

Key Terms
الفاعل الحكيم (al-fa'il al-hakim)
الفاعل الجاهل (al-fa'il al-jahil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's wisdom is compromised if He allows any evil.
Correction: Razi shows God's wisdom is preserved because He is not the initiator of the evil action; He only steers it to minimize harm.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why is the first objection not valid?
A) Because the agent is not wise but ignorant.
B) Because the world is not really originated.
C) Because God can do anything, even act without reason.
D) Because the objection is too weak to consider.

Key Takeaway
The first objection fails because it mistakenly assigns the initial act to God rather than to the ignorant soul.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you act out of ignorance and later see God redirecting that action for good, do you truly accept His excuse, or do you still cling to guilt and shame as if you had been the wise agent? How can you release that burden today?
?
Razi says the wise agent is excused when he cannot prevent the ignorant action. Is there someone in your life whose harmful behavior you cannot stop? Will you trust that God can redirect that situation—even through your own imperfect attempts—or will you insist on controlling the outcome?
?
This lesson distinguishes between two types of agents. Which are you in your daily decisions: the wise agent who acts with purpose, or the ignorant one who drifts? If the latter, what is one concrete step you will take today to act with intentionality before God?

First Objection: Does the Soul's Inclination Have a Cause?
Al-Razi rebuts the objection by turning it against the opponent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi presents and rebuts the objection that the soul's inclination must have a cause, and why the objection is turned back on the opponent.

Core Idea
The objection against al-Razi's view cuts both ways.

This lesson presents the first major objection to Muhammad ibn Zakariya al-Razi's doctrine of the soul's inclination. The objector challenges whether the soul's turning occurred without a cause. If it did, that undermines the proof of a Creator; if it did not, then why did the cause act at that specific moment? Al-Razi's answer cleverly turns the tables, showing that the objection applies equally to the objector's own beliefs about creation and to the philosophers' theory of celestial motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note the two parts: the objection and the answer.
The objection has a two-horned dilemma.
2
Identify the objection's logic
The objector asks: Did the inclination happen without a cause or from a cause? Trace both possibilities and their implications.
If no cause, then God's existence is disproven; if from a cause, why at that time?
3
Analyze al-Razi's response
Al-Razi does not directly answer; instead he shows that the same question applies to the objector's own view of creation and to the philosophers' gradual motion.
This is a dialectical tactic of consistency.
4
Reflect on the strategy
Consider how this objection and answer illustrate a key method in theological debates: turning the opponent's argument against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذه جملة الكلام في تقرير [ مذهب (۲) ] : محمد بن زكرياء الرازي . ولا بد (۳) بعد تقرير هذا الكلام من سؤالات وجوابات ليتضح مقصود الرجل من هذا الكلام : فالسؤال الأول : أن يقال : ذلك الالتفات الذي حصل لجوهر النفس ، حدث لا عن مؤثر ، أو عن مؤثر ؟ فإن كان الأول فقد حدث الحادث لا عن مؤثر ، وذلك يسد باب إثبات الصانع. وإن كان عن مؤثر فذلك المؤثر لم يفعل ذلك الخاطر قبل ذلك الوقت ؟ فإن كان ذلك لخاصية في ذلك الوقت، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : الفاعل [ الحكيم (۱) ] خص ذلك الوقت بالإحداث الخاصية فيه ؟ وإن كان لسبب آخر ، فلم لا يجوز مثله ههنا ؟ - أجاب : محمد بن زكرياء، عنه فقال : : إن هذا السؤال لازم على الكل . لانكم تقولون : إن الإله تعالى قصد إلى إيجاد العالم في ذلك الوقت المعين ، بعد أن كان تاركاً للفعل (۲) مدة غير متناهية . فإذا عقلتم هناك ، فلم لا يجوز مثله ههنا ؟ بل نقول : قد بينا : أن مثل هذا العبث والخراف ، البق بالجاهل السفيه منه بالحكيم العليم وأما الفلاسفة : فإنهم قالوا : إن الحركات الفلكية إنما حدثت جزءاً فجزءاً ، لأن كل حادث سابق ، يعد المحل لقبول الحادث اللاحق ، وهكذا لا إلى أول . وإذا عقل ذلك [ هناك (۳) ] فلم لا يعقل مثله ههنا ؟ .
This is the sum of the discourse in establishing the doctrine of Muhammad ibn Zakariya al-Razi. And after establishing this discourse, there must be questions and answers to clarify the intent of the man from this discourse. The first question: It is said: That inclination which occurred to the substance of the soul—did it occur without an effect [cause], or from an effect? If the first, then an event occurred without a cause, and that blocks the door of proving the Maker. And if from an effect, then why did that effect not produce that thought before that time? If that was due to a property in that time, then why is it not permissible to say that the wise agent specified that time with the property of bringing it about? And if it was for another reason, then why is the like not permissible here? Muhammad ibn Zakariya answered: Indeed, this question applies to everyone. Because you say that the exalted deity intended to bring the world into existence at that particular time after He had refrained from action for an infinite duration. Since you conceive of that there, why is the like not permissible here? Rather, we say: We have shown that such absurdity and nonsense is more befitting the ignorant fool than the wise knower. As for the philosophers, they said that the celestial movements occur part by part, because each preceding event prepares the substrate to accept the subsequent event, and so on without a beginning. And if that is conceivable there, why is the like not conceivable here?
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage presents a summary of al-Razi's doctrine and then the first objection and answer. The objection asks whether the soul's inclination (iltifat) happened without a cause or from a cause. If without, that undermines proving the Creator. If from a cause, why did that cause act at that specific time? The objector offers possibilities: either a special property in that time (so God could have chosen it) or another reason. Muhammad ibn Zakariya answers by turning the objection back: the objector's own belief that God created the world at a specific time after eternity faces the same problem. He also cites the philosophers' view of gradual celestial movements as an analogy.

Key Terms
التفات (inclination)
جوهر النفس (substance of soul)
مؤثر (effect/cause)
خاطر (thought)
خاصية (property)
حركات فلكية (celestial movements)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The answer defends al-Razi's view by providing a specific cause for the soul's inclination.
Correction: Al-Razi does not provide a cause; instead he argues that the objection equally plagues the opponent's own theory.

Checkpoint
What is the first possible scenario mentioned in the objector's question if the soul's inclination occurs from a cause?
A) The cause acted due to a property in that time
B) The cause acted due to the soul's free will
C) The cause acted due to divine command
D) The cause acted randomly

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi defends his view not by providing a cause for the soul's inclination, but by showing that the objection equally undermines the opponent's own position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are pressed to defend a belief, do you typically try to explain it or do you turn the challenge back on the challenger? Al-Razi chose the latter. Is that always valid in theological debate? Examine your own approach.
?
This lesson shows that even the greatest minds struggle with the 'why now' question regarding God's actions. Does this uncertainty shake your trust in philosophical reasoning, or does it drive you to rely more on revealed guidance? Where is your real confidence placed?
?
Al-Razi deflects the objection rather than providing a direct cause for the soul's inclination. If you were in his place, would you be satisfied with such a response? How willing are you to accept unresolved mysteries in your faith? What does that reveal about your intellectual humility?

Defending the Timing of the First Act
Objection and two answers on timing of first act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two arguments – a tu quoque from Muhammad ibn Zakariyya and an eternal sequence model from the philosophers – jointly rebut the objection that the first act's timing is arbitrary.

Core Idea
The objection about timing is turned back on the opponent and dissolved by sequential creation.

This passage presents an objection to the idea that God's first act of creation occurred at a specific moment. The objector argues that the timing must have a cause, but either way the argument leads to a regress. The response comes in two parts: first from Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, who shows the objection is self-refuting, and then from the philosophers, who model creation as an eternal sequential process without a first moment, thus sidestepping the issue.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection asks: why did the first act happen at that specific time? If due to a property of that time, why not attribute it to the agent; if due to another cause, why not apply the same reasoning elsewhere?
Note that the objector assumes the first act has a definite time.
2
Understand Muhammad ibn Zakariyya's response
He argues that the same question applies to the opponent, who also claims God created at a specific time after infinite inaction. Thus the objection is self-refuting. He adds that such absurd questioning fits only an ignorant fool.
This is a tu quoque (you too) argument.
3
Examine the philosophers' alternative model
The philosophers say celestial motions occur part by part without a first, each event preparing for the next. So there is no first time to question; the objection loses its force.
This model sidesteps the issue by denying a first moment entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يفعل ذلك الخاطر قبل ذلك الوقت ؟ فإن كان ذلك لخاصية في ذلك الوقت ، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : الفاعل [ الحكيم (۱) ] خص ذلك الوقت بالإحداث الخاصية فيه ؟ وإن كان لسبب آخر ، فلم لا يجوز مثله ههنا ؟ - أجاب : محمد بن زكرياء، عنه فقال : : إن هذا السؤال لازم على الكل . لانكم تقولون : إن الإله تعالى قصد إلى إيجاد العالم في ذلك الوقت المعين ، بعد أن كان تاركاً للفعل (۲) مدة غير متناهية . فإذا عقلتم هناك ، فلم لا يجوز مثله ههنا ؟ بل نقول : قد بينا : أن مثل هذا العبث والخراف ، البق بالجاهل السفيه منه بالحكيم العليم وأما الفلاسفة : فإنهم قالوا : إن الحركات الفلكية إنما حدثت جزءاً فجزءاً ، لأن كل حادث سابق ، يعد المحل لقبول الحادث اللاحق ، وهكذا لا إلى أول . وإذا عقل ذلك [ هناك (۳) ] فلم لا يعقل مثله ههنا ؟ . .
Does that thought occur before that time? If that is because of a specific property in that time, then why is it not permissible to say: the Wise Agent specified that time for the occurrence of the specific property? And if it is due to another cause, then why is the like of it not permissible here? - Muhammad ibn Zakariyya answered, saying: This question is necessary upon everyone. Because you say that the Exalted God intended to bring the world into existence at that specific time, after He had been refraining from action for an infinite duration. So if you accept that there, why is the like not permissible here? Rather, we say: we have shown that such absurdity and nonsense is more befitting of the ignorant fool than of the Wise, Knowing (agent). As for the philosophers: they said that the celestial movements only occurred part by part, because each preceding event prepares the locus for the reception of the subsequent event, and so on without a first. And if that is accepted there, why is the like not accepted here? ...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and a two-part answer concerning the timing of the first act of creation. The objection questions why the first act happened at a specific moment, suggesting that if it were due to a special property of that time, one could simply attribute that property to the agent, and if due to some other cause, the same logic should apply. The answer first comes from Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, who turns the question back against the opponent: the opponent himself claims God created the world at a particular time after infinite inaction, so the same question applies to him. He adds that such questioning is more fitting for an ignorant fool than for a wise, knowing agent. Then the philosophers provide a second answer: celestial motions are sequential without a beginning, each event preparing for the next, so the notion of a 'first' time does not arise; thus the objection is irrelevant. The passage thus defends the possibility of a specific first moment by using a tu quoque argument and a philosophical model of eternal sequential motion.

Key Terms
خاطر
خاصية
فاعل حكيم
حركات فلكية
حادث
محل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection proves that the first act's timing is arbitrary and cannot be explained.
Correction: The objection is turned back on the opponent (tu quoque) and is dissolved by the philosophers' model of eternal sequential creation without a first moment.

Checkpoint
What does Muhammad ibn Zakariyya argue in response to the question about the timing of the first act?

C) The philosophers have proven that time is eternal and without beginning.
D) The specific time is determined by the nature of the first act.

Key Takeaway
The timing of the first act is defended by showing the objection applies equally to the opponent and by positing a sequential creation without a first moment.

Answer to the Second Objection: Evil and the Foolish Agent
Refutation of the objection that a wise God uses a foolish agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends God's wisdom despite attributing the initiation of certain acts to an ignorant agent.

Core Idea
God uses an imperfect agent to initiate, but He is the source of all good.

This passage presents the second objection against the doctrine of divine causality and the author's response. The objector claims that if God is perfectly wise, He would not produce the world through a foolish agent. The answer explains that the presence of imperfection in the initial act prevents direct attribution to God, but all good proceeds from Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first part of the passage which states the objection: that a wise God would not act through a foolish agent.
Notice the phrase 'بعيد جدا' indicating the objector considers this absurd.
2
Understand the condition
The answer begins with a conditional: 'if these acts were free from all corruption, we would not need to attribute the beginning to the ignorant agent.'
This establishes that the acts are not free from corruption.
3
Note the three considerations
The author refers to three previously mentioned considerations that prevent attributing the beginning of the act directly to the Wise Agent.
These considerations are not detailed here but are assumed from earlier discussion.
4
See the attribution of good to God
After attributing the initiation to the ignorant agent, the author attributes all good, mercy, righteousness, and benefit to the Wise Merciful Agent.
This preserves God's role as the ultimate source of good.
5
Grasp the conclusion
On this assumption, God is merciful, benevolent, and deserving of endless praise.
The conclusion refutes the objection by showing God's wisdom and goodness are not compromised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسؤال الثاني : إن هذا الكلام يقتضي أن يكون الحكيم الكامل ، قصد إلى إيجاد هذا العالم الشريف، والأفعال الكاملة التامة ، تبعاً لفعل فاعل جاهل خسيس . وهو بعيد جدا أجاب عنه : « بأن هذه الأفعال الشريفة الكاملة ، لو كانت خالية عن [ جميع (4) ] جهات المفسدة والضرر ، لما كان بنا حاجة إلى إسناد أول الفعل إلى الفاعل الجاهل. أو لما دلت الوجوه الثلاثة المذكورة على أنه لا يجوز إسناد ابتداء هذا الفعل إلى الفاعل الحكيم، لا جرم قلنا : بأن المبتدىء بالفعل هو الفاعل الجاهل ، ثم أسندنا كل ما حصل في هذا العالم من الخير والرحمة والصلاح والمنفعة ، إلى الفاعل الحكيم الرحيم ، كان ذلك هو الواجب الذي لا محيص عنه . وعلى [ هذا (١) ] التقدير يكون الإله رحيماً محسناً ، ناظراً لعباده ، ساعياً في دفع الشرور عنهم ، وفي إيصال الخيرات إليهم ، فكان مستحقاً للحمد والشكر بغير نهاية ه .

That is extremely far-fetched. He answered: that these noble complete acts, if they were free from all aspects of corruption and harm, we would have no need to attribute the beginning of the act to the ignorant agent. That is what is necessary and unavoidable. And upon this assumption, God is merciful, benevolent, looking after His servants, striving to repel evils from them and to convey good things to them, so He deserves praise and gratitude without end.

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection and its answer. The objection argues that if the wise God's perfect acts result from the act of a foolish agent, that is absurd. The answer explains that the complete and perfect acts are not free from aspects of corruption; if they were, there would be no need to attribute the initiation to an ignorant agent. Moreover, the three previously mentioned considerations (implied earlier in the work) show that it is not permissible to attribute the beginning of these acts directly to the Wise Agent. So the author asserts that the beginner is indeed the ignorant agent, but then all the good, mercy, and benefit in the world are attributed to the Wise Merciful Agent. On this assumption, God is seen as merciful and benevolent, deserving endless praise. The key point is that the wise agent can use an intermediate agent for reasons that avoid direct attribution of imperfection.

Why God Did Not Prevent the Soul's Attachment to Hyle
Muhammad ibn Zakariyya answers why God allowed the soul's attachment to matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reasoning behind why God allowed the soul's attachment to matter despite foreseeing the resulting afflictions.

Core Idea
Some evils are impossible to prevent by divine decree, so God orchestrates the best possible outcome.

In this passage, an objection is raised: if God knew the soul's attachment to matter would cause suffering, why didn't He prevent it? The answer reveals a key insight about divine power and the nature of the soul. We will see why preventing the attachment was impossible, and how God still exercises wisdom by arranging the best possible configuration and granting intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objection is framed: it assumes God could have prevented evil. The answer responds with two key points.
The passage begins with 'The fourth question' and ends with 'Rather, this...' (incomplete).
2
Identify the two arguments in the answer
The answer has two parts: 1) The soul's love for matter is an essential instinct, so removing it is impossible—God only has power over the possible. 2) Even if God tried to prevent it, the soul would not comply; instead, God allowed the attachment but then arranged compositions to maximize good and minimize evil, and gave the intellect to guide the soul.
These arguments defend God's wisdom and mercy.
3
Reflect on how this defends divine goodness
Consider how the answer addresses the theological problem of evil: it shows that some evils arise from necessary properties of creation, not from God's failure to prevent them. God's power is limited to the possible, and He actively brings about the best possible world.
This connects to broader discussions of divine attributes and causality in Kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الرابع (4) ] : قالوا : لما علم الإله (*) أن تعلق النفس بالهيولي ، يوجب فتح باب الآفات والمخافات ، فلم لم يمنع النفس من ذلك التعلق ؟ أجاب : محمد بن زكرياء ، عنه : : بأن ذلك العشق ، لما صار ذاتياً غريزياً الجوهر النفس ، كانت إزالة ذلك العشق ممتنعة ، والبارى تعالى إنما يقدر على الممكن ، لا على الممتنع . فعلم (٦) الله تعالى أنه لو منع النفس عن التعلق بالهيولى ، لم تمتنع عن ذلك التعلق ، ولم تنقطع مادة ذلك الشر . فلهذا السبب لم يقصد الإله الحكيم [ الرحيم (٧) ] منع النفس عن التعلق بالهيولى ، بل تركها حتى تعلقت بها ، ثم أوقع تلك التركيبات على الوجه الذي يكون أقرب إلى الخير والصلاح ، وأبعد عن الشر والفساد . ثم أفاض البارىء على جـوهـر النفس : نور العقل ، حتى أن النفس بقوة نور العقل وبكثرة التجارب لأحوال هذا العالم ، تعرف أنه لا فائدة في [ تعلقها (۸) ] بهذه الهيولى البتة . بل هذا
The fourth question: They said: Since God knew that the soul's attachment to hyle (prime matter) necessitates opening the door of afflictions and fears, why did He not prevent the soul from that attachment? Muhammad ibn Zakariyya answered: that that love, when it became an essential instinct of the substance of the soul, its removal was impossible, and the Exalted Creator is only able over the possible, not the impossible. So God knew that if He prevented the soul from attachment to hyle, it would not refrain from that attachment, and the material of that evil would not cease. For this reason, the Wise Merciful God did not intend to prevent the soul from attachment to hyle, but He left it until it became attached to it, then He brought about those compositions in the way that is closest to good and righteousness and farthest from evil and corruption. Then the Creator poured upon the substance of the soul the light of intellect, so that the soul, by the power of the light of intellect and by many experiences of the states of this world, knows that there is no benefit at all in its attachment to this hyle. Rather, this...
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection and its answer. The objection is a theological problem: if God knew that the soul's attachment to matter causes suffering, why did He not prevent it? The answer, attributed to Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, asserts that the soul's love for matter is an essential, instinctual property of its substance, making its removal impossible. God is only able over what is possible, not the impossible. Moreover, even if God attempted to prevent the attachment, the soul would not comply, and evil would continue. So God allowed the attachment but then arranged the compositions in the best possible way to maximize good and minimize evil. Additionally, God granted the soul the light of intellect so that through reason and experience, the soul can come to recognize the futility of its attachment and thereby purify itself. The answer thus defends God's wisdom and mercy by appealing to the nature of the soul and the limits of divine power regarding impossibilities.

نور العقل
تركيبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could have prevented all evil simply by willing it, so He is responsible for suffering.
Correction: The soul's love for matter is an essential property, making its prevention impossible (ممتنع). God's power only extends to the possible, and He actively arranges creation to bring about the best possible outcome.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Philosophers' Rejection of Razi's Mazhab
States that philosophers who affirm emanation reject this mazhab because it assumes a free agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why certain philosophers reject Razi's mazhab due to their belief in God's necessary emanation and denial of free agency.

Core Idea
Philosophers who deny free will reject any doctrine built on it.

This lesson explains a key doctrinal divide: philosophers who hold that God's action is necessary by essence cannot accept a mazhab that presumes a free agent. The passage links Razi's mazhab to the free agent theory, showing why its rejection is inevitable from their perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic and its translation to get the full argument.
Notice the logical flow: premise, reason, conclusion.
2
Identify the key concepts
Focus on the terms 'وَجِبٌ بِالذات' (necessary by essence) and 'الفاعل المختار' (free agent). Understand how they oppose each other.
3
Analyze the conclusion
The author states that philosophers' denial of this mazhab is even stronger because it is a branch of a theory they reject at its root.
Consider why this rejection is 'stronger'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن الفلاسفة الذين يقولون بأن إله العالم موجب بالذات ينكرون هذا المذهب . لأجل أنه من فروع القائلين بالفاعل المختار . والفلاسفة ينكرون القول بالفاعل المختار ، فوجب أن يكون إنكارهم لهذا القول أشد
And know that the philosophers who say that the god of the world is necessary by essence (wajib bi al-dhat) deny this doctrine, because it is from the branches of those who affirm the free agent (al-fa'il al-mukhtar). And the philosophers deny the statement of the free agent, so it is necessary that their denial of this statement is stronger.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage explains why a certain group of philosophers reject Razi's doctrine. These philosophers hold that God is 'wajib bi al-dhat' — His existence is necessary by virtue of His essence, and His actions are necessitated, not chosen freely. They reject the concept of a free agent (al-fa'il al-mukhtar) who acts by will and choice. The author notes that Razi's doctrine is a branch of the free agent theory, i.e., it presupposes that God is a free agent who can choose to create or not, and to act in certain ways. Therefore, since these philosophers deny the very foundation of the free agent, their rejection of this specific doctrine is even stronger.

Key Terms
الفلاسفة
موجب بالذات
الفاعل المختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All philosophers reject Razi's mazhab.
Correction: Only those who deny the free agent do so; philosophers who affirm free will may accept it.

Checkpoint

B) Because it is a branch of the free agent theory, which they deny.
C) Because it is based on rational good and evil.
D) Because they affirm the eternity of the world.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers who see God as necessitated by His essence reject Razi's mazhab because it is rooted in the free agent theory which they deny.

Refutation of Recompense for Tiny Animals
The author refutes the view that God must recompense all creatures, especially tiny ones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that God must recompense all creatures, especially tiny animals, and the refutation based on forgetfulness and the weakness of rational beautification.

Core Idea
God is not obligated to recompense animals that forget their suffering.

In this passage, the author tackles a specific Mu'tazilite claim that God must resurrect and recompense even the tiniest animals. The proponents argue that angels and jinn observe the suffering, so there is a moral lesson. The author dismisses this as a corollary of the flawed principle of rational beautification and presents a counter-argument based on forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal English translation. Get a sense of the author's argument before analyzing details.
2
Identify the proponents' claim
The proponents argue that tiny animals must be recompensed because angels, jinn, and devils observe their suffering. Note how they make it obligatory upon God.
This claim is based on the Mu'tazilite principle of rational beautification and vilification (tahsin wa taqbih).
3
Understand the author's classification
The author labels this argument as a ramification of tahsin wa taqbih, which he has previously shown to be weak. Recognize that this is his core refutation.
The author does not repeat the detailed refutation here but refers to prior knowledge.
4
Analyze the forgetfulness counterargument
Some investigators argue that if an animal suffers, is resurrected after a long time and forgets the pain, the reward is like a new blessing, not compensation for past harm. This severs the link between the original injury and the recompense.
This undermines the need for recompense: if the animal doesn't remember, there's no point in compensating.
5
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author dismisses the lengthy Mu'tazilite discussion as weak and chooses brevity. Consider why he does not engage further.
The author's approach is to expose the foundational error (tahsin wa taqbih) rather than argue details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن الحيوانات التي تكون في غاية الصغر ، قد تتولد في قعور البحور ودواخل الأرض ، بحيث لا يطلع عليها أحد، فكيف يحصل الاعتبار بإيصال الألام إليها ؟ أجابوا : بأن الملائكة والجن والشياطين يشاهدونها ، فيحصل لهم أنواع من الاعتبارات في الدين. ثم إن القائلين بهذا القول ، أوجبوا على الله تعالى : حشر جميع البق والبراغيث والقمل والديدان ، وإيصال الأعواض إليها. وزعموا أنه لو أخل بإعادة شيء منها لصار سفيهاً ومعزولاً عن الإلهية. واعلم : أن هذا من تفاريع تحسين العقل وتقبيحه . وقد علمت ضعفه وسقوطه . وقال بعض المحققين : إنه إذا وصل الضرر إلى حيوان ، ثم إنه يعاد ذلك الحيوان بعد عشرة آلاف سنة ، وتلك الحالة قد نسيها ذلك الحيوان ، ولم يبق له بها شعور ، كان ذلك الإنعام جارياً مجرى الإنعام المبتدأ ، ويصير منقطع التعلق عما مضى ولما طال كلام المعتزلة في تفاصيل هذا الباب طولاً مقروناً بالضعف والرخاوة . لا جرم أثرنا الاختصار فيه [ والله أعلم ] .
Indeed, the animals that are extremely small may be generated in the depths of the seas and the interiors of the earth, such that no one observes them. So how can taking heed occur by inflicting pains upon them? They answered: The angels, jinn, and devils observe them, so they obtain various types of considerations in religion. Then those who hold this view made it obligatory upon God Almighty to gather all bugs, fleas, lice, and worms, and to deliver recompense (al-a'wad) to them. They claimed that if He failed to bring any of them back, He would become foolish and disqualified from divinity. Know that this is among the ramifications of the doctrine of rational beautification and vilification (tahsin al-'aql wa taqbihihi). And you have known its weakness and fallaciousness. And some investigators said: If harm reaches an animal, then that animal is brought back after ten thousand years, and that state has been forgotten by that animal and leaves no awareness in it, then that beneficence is like the original beneficence, and its connection to the past is severed. And since the speech of the Mu'tazila on the details of this topic was lengthy, coupled with weakness and flimsiness, we have preferred brevity concerning it. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that God is obligated to recompense all animals, including the tiniest ones. The author first presents the proponents' argument: even if humans don't see the pain inflicted on microscopic animals, angels, jinn, and devils observe it and gain moral lessons. Then the proponents go further, asserting that God must resurrect all such creatures and deliver recompense to them, otherwise He would be foolish and unworthy of divinity. The author labels this as a corollary of the Mu'tazilite principle of rational beautification and vilification (tahsin wa taqbih), which he considers weak. He then offers a counter-argument by some investigators: if an animal suffers, then is resurrected after ten thousand years with no memory of the pain, the reward is essentially a new blessing, disconnected from the past injury. Finally, the author dismisses the elaborate Mu'tazilite discussion on this topic as lengthy and weak, opting for brevity.

Key Terms
أعواض
إعادة
تحسين وتقبيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God is obligated to recompense every animal that suffers, including tiny ones, otherwise He would be unjust or foolish.
Correction: The obligation is based on the flawed principle of rational beautification; moreover, if the animal forgets the suffering, the reward is a new blessing, not compensation.

Checkpoint

C) There is no benefit needed

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite argument for mandatory recompense of tiny animals is refuted by exposing its foundation in rational beautification and by the forgetfulness counterargument.

The Infinite Regress Argument Against Deniers of Rational Good and Evil
Final proof that denying rational good and evil entails no specifier for creation's time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying rational good and evil forces one to accept an infinite regress and thus fail to specify the time of creation.

Core Idea
Denying rational good and evil leads to creation without a specifier — an impossibility.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi delivers the final blow to those who deny that reason can discern good and evil. He shows that their position leads to an absurd infinite regress, forcing them to say God created the world at a specific time with absolutely no reason or specifier. This argument completes the chapter's investigation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify its key components.
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the author's claim about the cause and the refutation of the third option.
This passage is a compact argument.
2
Understand the infinite regress argument.
The author argues that if the specification of time had a cause, it would lead to an infinite chain. Grasp the two forms of regress: simultaneous or sequential.
The regress is impossible because it implies an infinite number of past events.
3
See the conclusion forced upon the opponent.
The opponent must say that God's act of creation had no reason or specifier — a statement they would reject.
This shows the necessity of rational good and evil.
4
Reflect on the significance of this argument.
Consider how this argument serves as a reductio ad absurdum, proving that rational discernment is necessary for causality.
The argument completes the chapter's investigation.

المقتضى لتلك الخاصية ، شيء من لوازم ذلك الوقت ومن مقتضياته . والثالث باطل . لأنا كما قلنا : ما المقتضى لاختصاص ذلك الوقت بحدوث العالم فيه ؟ وكذلك ما المقتضى لاختصاص ذلك الوقت بتلك الخاصية ؟ ويلزم التسلسل . إما دفعة واحدة، وإما واحداً قبل آخر ، لا إلى أول . وذلك يقتضي حدوث حوادث لا أول لها . فثبت : أن القائلين بنفي تحسين العقل وتقبيحه ، يلزمهم أن يقولوا : إنه تعالى خصص إحداث العالم بذلك الوقت المعين ، لا لمخصص أصلاً البتة . وهذا تمام المباحث في هذا الباب
The cause for that property is something from the necessary concomitants of that time and from its requirements. And the third is false. For we said: What is the cause for the specification of that time for the occurrence of the world? And likewise what is the cause for the specification of that time with that property? This leads to an infinite regress: either all at once, or one after another with no first. That necessitates the occurrence of accidents with no first. So it is established that those who deny rational good and evil are forced to say that He, exalted, specified the bringing about of the world in that particular time with absolutely no specifier at all. And this completes the investigations in this chapter.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage presents the final proof in a refutation of those who deny that reason discerns good and evil (taḥsīn al-ʿaql wa taqbīḥuh). The argument is a critique of their position regarding the specification of the time of creation. The author, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, states that the cause (muqtaḍā) for a particular property is something from the necessary concomitants (lawāzim) and requirements (muqtaḍayāt) of that time. He then says the third option (presumably in a previous enumeration of possibilities) is false. This is because, as previously stated, there is no cause for the specification of that particular time for the occurrence of the world, nor for the specification of that time with that property. This leads to an infinite regress (tasalsul), either all at once or sequentially with no first, implying the occurrence of infinite accidents (ḥawādith lā awwal lahā). The conclusion is that those who deny rational good and evil must say that God specified the creation of the world in that particular time with absolutely no specifier (lā mukhassiṣ aṣlan), which is absurd. The passage ends by marking the completion of the chapter.

Key Terms
المقتضى (al-muqtaḍā)
اللازم (al-lāzim)
التسلسل (al-tasalsul)
المخصص (al-mukhassiṣ)
تحسين العقل وتقبيحه (taḥsīn al-ʿaql wa taqbīḥuh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular.
Correction: It is a reductio ad absurdum showing the opponent's position leads to an absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do those who deny rational good and evil end up saying about God's creation of the world?
A) God created the world in the best possible time.
B) God specified the time of creation without any specifier at all.
C) God created the world in multiple times.
D) God's creation is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Denying rational good and evil forces one to accept that God created the world at a specific time without any reason, which is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God has a wise purpose in everything He creates, including the specific time of your own existence? If so, how does that shape your view of events that seem random or unjust in your life?
?
If you were to deny that good and evil are rationally discernible, would you be comfortable with the idea that God's commands could be arbitrary? How would that affect your relationship with Him and your motivation to obey?
?
The argument shows that denying a moral order leads to an irrational conclusion about creation. Reflect: In what areas of your life are you tempted to act as if there is no objective moral order? What would it mean to live consistently with the belief that God's creation is purposeful and rationally discernible?
